\newcommand{\storybox}[3]{% #1=x, #2=y, #3=text
  \begin{textblock}{3}(#1,#2)
    \noindent%
    \begin{tikzpicture}
      \node[rectangle, rounded corners=3pt, fill=white, inner sep=0.1in, text width=2.55in, align=left] {%
        \small\sffamily #3%
      };
    \end{tikzpicture}%
  \end{textblock}%
}

{\Large\sffamily A Speculative Atlas of Climate Disaster}

\vspace{0.5in}

{\large\sffamily A Procedurally Generated Novel}

{\large\sffamily by Mark Sample}

\vfill

{\normalsize\sffamily Generated November 24, 2025}

% About page
\newpage
\section*{About This Novel}

\noindent\textit{No Time to Discourse} is a speculative atlas that explores climate disaster across North America through interactive mapping and generative flash fiction.

\vspace{0.3in}

\noindent This novel was generated for NaNoGenMo (National Novel Generation Month), transforming the web-based interactive experience of https://notime.now/ into a print format. Each page combines watercolor maps from Stamen Design with works of flash fiction, which are procedurally-generated through bespoke RiTa.js grammars developed by Mark Sample.

\vspace{0.3in}

\noindent Each of the stories in this novel is a work of fiction, yet each also attempts to capture at a human level the realities of climate disaster.

\vspace{0.3in}

\noindent\textbf{Original Web Project:} \url{https://notime.now/}

\noindent\textbf{Code Repository:} \url{https://github.com/samplereality/no-time-to-discourse-novel}

\clearpage

% Henry V quote on its own page
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
  {\Large\textit{"The day is hot, and the weather, and the wars, and the King,\\
  and the Dukes; it is no time to discourse."}}

  \vspace{0.3in}

  --- Henry V
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\storybox{1.68}{8.00}{\textbf{Gila Bend, Arizona}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Monday, March 9, 2026}\\
 The storm came suddenly, in a furious blur. The sky over Gila Bend darkened. Adrien had a fleeting thought, that evil was rising. Somewhere in Gila Bend, twenty years of Arturo's life floated away in cardboard boxes. The clocks stopped at 5:18 AM.}

\storybox{0.47}{4.35}{\textbf{Glendale, Arizona}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Monday, July 16, 2029}\\
 The storm had been brewing for days. The barometer was dropping. The air was thick. When the storm finally came to Glendale, it was apocalyptic. Jasper watched as the storm pounded Arrowhead Ranch. The lights were out for weeks. They trucked in bottled water, since nothing was safe to drink.}

\storybox{4.80}{4.66}{\textbf{Phoenix, Arizona}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Monday, December 28, 2026}\\
 The wells run dry, and a foul layer of dust covers Papago Park. Weathered docks roast uncovered in the  sun. The crops are dead. It's like the surface of the moon, thinks Mara. It hasn't rained in what feels like years. She can't take much more of this.}

\storybox{4.64}{7.74}{\textbf{Springfield, Massachusetts}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Saturday, July 29, 2028}\\
 The soil is cracked, and the fire department had to truck in water to fill their tanks. Tangles of trash bake  in the scorching sun. The livestock are dead. It's like the surface of the moon, thinks Yamileth. It hasn't rained in months. Meaningless words tumble around in her head. \textit{Threesome, vinegars. Headdress}.}

\storybox{0.41}{7.98}{\textbf{Hartford, Connecticut}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Thursday, July 16, 2026}\\
 Kathleen saw the relentless water wash away trees, sidewalks, whole communities. Aqui Me Quedo. There's too much water and yet not enough water, reflects Jordyn. She didn't think it would be this bad. Paramedic teams are nowhere to be seen. }

\storybox{2.01}{4.45}{\textbf{Waterbury, Connecticut}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Thursday, July 6, 2028}\\
 Wildfires rage in the hills. Hundreds of thousands of acres are already destroyed. The exhaustion Mariyah feels, she's been up for days, riding shotgun on the helitack crew. The copter rotors beat endlessly above the burning world.}

\storybox{5.33}{3.83}{\textbf{Leesburg, Florida}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Wednesday, November 3, 2027}\\
 This year's low tide is higher than last year's high tide. Pythons are everywhere.}

\storybox{3.19}{0.50}{\textbf{Ocala, Florida}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Friday, October 20, 2028}\\
 Hurricane Aislinn roared ashore as a Category 5 monster, catching meteorologists off guard. Ezra evacuated to a friend's house three states away with only what fit in the car. He called neighbors who didn't answer, wondering if his house would survive. The hurricane redefined geography. Streets became rivers, parking lots lakes, and home was just a GPS coordinate in the middle of nowhere. He couldn't stop refreshing the missing persons list, looking for names he recognized.}

\storybox{1.55}{4.39}{\textbf{Gainesville, Florida}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Saturday, January 31, 2026}\\
 Hurricane Payton intensified over the warm Gulf waters, following the path forecasters feared most. Payton decided to stay, having survived Andrew in '92. Now he wished he'd listened as windows exploded inward. Volunteers in fishing boats found him clinging to floating debris. Congress appropriated \$75 million for a military parade on the President's birthday.}

\storybox{4.66}{4.55}{\textbf{Key West, Florida}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Wednesday, March 1, 2028}\\
 Hurricane Freya roared ashore as a Category 5 monster, defying every computer model. Mateo evacuated to a church basement with only what fit in the car. He watched the news obsessively, wondering if his cat who wouldn't come out from under the bed would survive. He spent eighteen hours on a highway overpass with forty strangers, sharing the last bottle of water while waiting for help that came three days late. On social media the President bragged about his new plane.}

\storybox{1.02}{7.05}{\textbf{Homestead, Florida}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Sunday, July 19, 2026}\\
 Hurricane Lila roared ashore as a Category 5 monster, defying every computer model. Lila hunkered down in her home, praying silently as the water stripped bark from trees beside the the roof she'd been meaning to repair. The storm left behind a landscape of snapped power lines and roofless houses. She laughed bitterly at the FEMA trailer's mold problem---at least it was consistent.}
